TADI                                                                                       iii
          CHAPTER I ­ INTRODUCTION & EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
PART A ­ PURPOSE OF REPORT AND STUDY OBJECTIVES
Christian Chapel & School is proposed to be located west of STH 83, east of Nagawicka Road,
and south of Cardinal Lane in the City of Delafield, Waukesha County. TADI conducted this
TIA to determine the expected weekday peak hour operating conditions and recommendations at
identified study area intersections.
This report documents the procedures, findings and conclusions of the traffic impact analysis.
The analysis identifies recommended improvements based on existing roadway conditions,
existing traffic volumes, and additional traffic expected to be generated by the proposed
Christian Chapel & School.
PART B ­ EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
The executive summary includes a description of the study area, description of the development
and conclusions based on the findings of the TIA.
B1. Location of Study Site with Respect to Area Roadway Network
A street map illustrating the location of the proposed Christian Chapel & School is shown in
Exhibit 1-1. A conceptual site plan is shown in Exhibit 1-2. The site is currently utilized for
agricultural purposes. A small neighborhood exists along Faire Lakes Parkway to the west of the
site, and another second small neighborhood exists along Campbell Terrace Road to the
northwest of the site.
The study area for this TIA includes the following:
           STH 83 & Cardinal Lane (traffic signal control); and
           Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway (two-way stop control).
No immediate transportation improvement projects were identified within the study area.
B2. On-Site Development Description
Christian Chapel & School is proposed to serve as a sanctuary with 850-900 seats as well as a
private K-8 school with an estimated full build-out population of 370 students. The school is
expected to be the primary source of traffic during weekdays.
For the purpose of analyzing traffic impacts, the full-build completion of the site was assumed to
occur under one phase in the Year 2013. The actual timeline for completion and operation will
vary.
B3. Off-Site Development Description
No off-site developments were identified.
B4. Site Generated Traffic
To address any potential future traffic impacts at the study area intersections, it is necessary to
identify the hourly volume of traffic generated by anticipated development. The traffic volumes
expected to be generated by the Christian Chapel & School are based on the size and type of the
proposed use and on trip rates as published in the Institute of Transportation Engineers' (ITE)
Trip Generation Manual, Ninth Edition, 2012.
The full build-out of the Christian Chapel & School is expected to result in approximately 335
new trips (185 in/150 out) during a typical weekday morning pear hour of school arrival, 220
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                          April 10, 2013

new trips (105 in/115 out) during a typical weekday midday peak hour of school dismissal, and
110 new trips (55 in/55 out) during a typical weekday evening peak hour.
B5. Proposed Development Access
Primary access to the Christian Chapel & School is planned to STH 83 via an extension of
Cardinal Lane.
The City of Delafield 2030 Comprehensive Plan envisions a future collector street connecting
Cardinal Lane to Faire Lakes Parkway. For the purpose of this study, two scenarios were
developed:
       Under Scenario One, a future collector street connection does not exist. All access is
       accommodated via STH 83.
       Under Scenario Two, a future secondary access is assumed to Nagawicka Road via a
       connection of Faire Lakes Parkway to Cardinal Lane.
A recommendation regarding the two scenarios is summarized at the end of this chapter.
B6. Existing Traffic Recommended Improvements
The study area intersections were analyzed based on the procedures set forth in the 2000
Highway Capacity Manual (HCM). Intersection operation is defined by "level of service".
Level of Service (LOS) is a quantitative measure that refers to the overall quality of flow at an
intersection ranging from very good, represented by LOS `A', to very poor, represented by LOS
`F'. For the purpose of this study, and as is standard for use in the WisDOT Southeast Region,
LOS D or better was used to define desirable peak hour operating conditions.
The following improvements are recommended to accommodate the Year 2013 existing (without
development) traffic volumes. These improvements are in addition to conditions as they
currently exist and are recommended regardless of any new development in the area.
Improvements are for jurisdictional consideration and are not legally binding. WisDOT and the
City of Delafield reserve the right to determine alternative solutions.
       STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
           No improvements are expected to be necessary.
       Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway
           TADI performed a speed study along Nagawicka Road at Faire Lakes Parkway.
             The 85th percentile speed was found to be 33-mph. The results suggest that the
             existing posted speed limit of 30 mph on Nagawicka Road is reasonable.
               TADI performed an intersection sight distance (ISD) study for the Nagawicka
               Road intersection with Faire Lakes Parkway. The study revealed that ISD is not
               currently provided from Faire Lakes Parkway to Nagawicka Road. It is
               recommended to clear all trees, brush and other obstructions from within the ISD
               envelope.
               TADI learned that a crash involving more than one fatality occurred at the
               intersection due to a loss of vehicle control within the last one to three years, and
               another fatality occurred at the intersection approximately fifteen years ago. To
               improve the safety of the intersection, countermeasures such as wider shoulders
               with rumble strips, "curve ahead" signs, and/or a lighted intersection should be
               considered within the intersection influence area.


TADI                                                                                                   2
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                        April 10, 2013

B7. Build Traffic Recommended Improvements
The following improvements, shown in Exhibit 1-3, are recommended to accommodate the Year
2013 build (with Christian Chapel & School) traffic volumes regardless of whether or not a
collector street connection is made between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway. These
improvements are in addition to conditions as they currently exist. Improvements are for
jurisdictional consideration and are not legally binding. WisDOT and the City of Delafield
reserve the right to determine alternative solutions.
       STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
           Construct a right-turn lane on the STH 83 southbound approach.
               Provide two lanes on the Cardinal Lane eastbound approach, including one left-
               turn lane and a shared through/right-turn lane. Align the center of the eastbound
               left-turn lane with the center of the existing westbound left-turn lane to improve
               sight distance for left-turn motorists at the intersection.
       Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway
           No improvements are expected to be necessary beyond those recommended to
             accommodate existing traffic volumes.
       Other Considerations
           Install stop signs to control the northbound and southbound frontage road
              approaches to Cardinal Lane.
               Roadways to/from the development may be constructed as two-lane undivided
               facilities.
               It is recommended to move forward with the proposed development without the
               collector roadway connection between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway.
                   o A collector connection is not necessary, as the connection would not
                     provide a substantial benefit to the proposed Christian Chapel & School,
                     to the STH 83 & Cardinal Lane intersection, or the Nagawicka Road &
                     Faire Lakes Parkway intersection.
                   o A collector connection is expected to increase traffic along Nagawicka
                     Road at Faire Lakes Parkway rather than relieve it.
                   o Nagawicka Road currently operates at LOS B and has excess capacity to
                     accommodate 2.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS C/D
                     threshold. With land along Nagawicka Road nearly fully built-out today,
                     future development opportunities along Nagawicka Road are not expected
                     to result in traffic concerns that would drive the need for a collector
                     connection.
B8. Conclusion
All movements at the study area intersections are expected to operate safely and efficiently with
the identified recommended improvements.
It is recommended to move forward with the proposed development without the collector
roadway connection between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway, for the following reasons:
       A collector connection is not necessary, as the connection would not provide a substantial
       benefit to the proposed Christian Chapel & School, to the STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
       intersection, or the Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway intersection.
TADI                                                                                                3
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                      April 10, 2013

       A collector connection is expected to increase traffic along Nagawicka Road at Faire
       Lakes Parkway rather than relieve it.
       Nagawicka Road currently operates at LOS B and has excess capacity to accommodate
       2.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS C/D threshold. With land along
       Nagawicka Road nearly fully built-out today, future development opportunities along
       Nagawicka Road are not expected to result in traffic concerns that would drive the need
       for a collector connection.

                   CHAPTER II ­ PROPOSED DEVELOPMENT
PART A ­ ON-SITE DEVELOPMENT
A1. Development Description and Site Location
Christian Chapel & School is proposed to be located west of STH 83, east of Nagawicka Road,
and south of Cardinal Lane in the City of Delafield, Waukesha County. A street map illustrating
the location of the proposed Christian Chapel & School is shown in Exhibit 2-1. A conceptual
site plan is shown in Exhibit 2-2.
A small neighborhood exists along Faire Lakes Parkway to the west of the site, and second small
neighborhood exists along Campbell Terrace Road to the northwest of the site.
A2. Land Use and Intensity
Christian Chapel & School is proposed to serve as a sanctuary with 850-900 seats as well as a
private K-8 school with an estimated full build-out population of 370 students. The school is
expected to be the primary source of traffic during weekdays.
A3. Site Plan
Primary access to the Christian Chapel & School is planned to STH 83 via an extension of
Cardinal Lane.
The City of Delafield 2030 Comprehensive Plan envisions a future collector street connecting
Cardinal Lane to Faire Lakes Parkway. For the purpose of this study, two scenarios were
developed:
       Under Scenario One, a future collector street connection does not exist. All access is
       accommodated via STH 83.
       Under Scenario Two, a future secondary access is assumed to Nagawicka Road via a
       connection of Faire Lakes Parkway to Cardinal Lane.
A recommendation regarding the two scenarios is summarized at the end of Chapter I and of
Chapter VI.
A4. Development Phasing and Timing
For the purpose of analyzing traffic impacts, the full-build completion of the Christian Chapel &
School was assumed to occur under one phase in the Year 2013. The actual timeline for
completion and operation will vary.
PART B ­ STUDY AREA
B1. Influence Area
The primary influence area for the Christian Chapel & School is the City of Delafield and other
area Lake Country communities. The proposed school is expected to have a regional draw.
B2. Area of Significant Traffic Impact
The study area for this TIA includes the following:
           STH 83 & Cardinal Lane (traffic signal control); and
           Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway (two-way stop control).
PART C ­ OFF-SITE LAND USE AND DEVELOPMENT
No off-site developments were identified.

TADI                                                                                              5
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                        April 10, 2013

PART D ­ SITE ACCESSIBILITY
D1. Study Area Roadways
The study area roadways are discussed below:
STH 83 is a two-lane undivided north/south arterial highway with a rural cross-section and
interchange access to USH 16 to the north and I-94 to the south. The 2009 WisDOT annual
average daily traffic (AADT) volumes on STH 83 were 14,400 vehicles per day (vpd) north of
Cardinal Lane and 13,200 vpd south of Cardinal Lane. The posted speed limit along STH 83 is
45 mph.
Cardinal Lane is a two-lane east/west roadway with a posted speed limit of 30 mph. The
roadway has a rural cross-section west of STH 83 and an urban cross-section east of STH 83.
According to the WisDOT, the Year 2009 annual average daily traffic (AADT) volume on
Cardinal Lane was about 7,100 vehicles per day (vpd) immediately east of STH 83.
Nagawicka Road is a two-lane north/south roadway with rural cross-section and a posted speed
limit of 30 mph. AADT volumes are not recorded for Nagawicka Road.
Faire Lakes Parkway is a two-lane east-west roadway with rural cross-section, no outlet, and an
unposted but implied speed limit of 25 mph. AADT volumes are not recorded for Faire Lakes
Parkway.
D2. Additional Modes of Transportation
No pedestrian or bicycle facilities were identified in the study area. No regularly scheduled
transit exists in the study area.
D3. Anticipated Improvement Projects
No immediate transportation improvement projects were identified within the study area.

           CHAPTER III ­ ANALYSIS OF EXISTING CONDITIONS
PART A ­ PHYSICAL CHARACTERISTICS
A transportation detail showing existing lane configurations, traffic controls and posted speed
limits is included in Exhibit 3-1. No immediate transportation improvement projects were
identified within the study area.
PART B ­ TRAFFIC VOLUMES
The following table outlines the dates that turning movement traffic counts were collected at the
study area intersections. All counts were collected by TADI.
       Intersection                             Wkday AM     Wkday MID        Wkday PM
       STH 83 & Cardinal Lane                   Wed 2-6-13     Tue 2-5-13      Tue 2-5-13
       Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Pkwy        Wed 2-6-13     Tue 2-5-13      Tue 2-5-13

Based on the available turning movement counts, the weekday morning and weekday evening
peak hours were identified as being 7:30 to 8:30am and 4:30 to 5:30pm. A "midday" peak hour
has been identified to coincide with the peak school dismissal peak hour. The weekday midday
peak hour was identified as being 3:00 to 4:00pm.
The traffic counts were taken in early February of 2013 and were seasonally adjusted by a factor
of 1.093 (from WisDOT Daily & Seasonal Factors for 2011). The seasonally adjusted Year
2013 existing traffic volumes are shown in Exhibit 3-2.
PART C ­ INTERSECTION LEVEL OF SERVICE
C1. Level of Service Definitions
The study area intersections were analyzed based on the procedures set forth in the 2000
Highway Capacity Manual (HCM). Intersection operation is defined by "level of service".
Level of service (LOS) is a quantitative measure that refers to the overall quality of flow at an
intersection ranging from very good, represented by LOS `A', to very poor, represented by LOS
`F'. For the purpose of this study, LOS D was used to define desirable peak hour operating
conditions. Descriptions of the various levels of service are as follows:
       LOS A is the highest level of service that can be achieved. Under this condition,
       intersection approaches appear quite open, turning movements are easily made, and
       nearly all drivers find freedom of operation. At signalized and unsignalized intersections,
       average delays are less than 10 seconds.
       LOS B represents stable operation. At signalized intersections, average vehicle delays are
       10 to 20 seconds. At unsignalized intersections, average delays are 10 to 15 seconds.
       LOS C still represents stable operation, but periodic backups of a few vehicles may
       develop behind turning vehicles. Most drivers begin to feel restricted, but not
       objectionably so. At signalized intersections, average vehicle delays are 20 to 35
       seconds. At unsignalized intersections, average delays are 15 to 25 seconds.
       LOS D represents increasing traffic restrictions as the intersection approaches instability.
       Delays to approaching vehicles may be substantial during short peaks within the peak
       period, but periodic clearance of long lines occurs, thus preventing excessive backups.
       At signalized intersections, average vehicle delays are 35 to 55 seconds. At unsignalized
       intersections, average delays are 25 to 35 seconds.



TADI                                                                                                7
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                        April 10, 2013

       LOS E represents the capacity of the intersection. At signalized intersections, average
       vehicle delays are 55 to 80 seconds. At unsignalized intersections, average delays are 35
       to 50 seconds.
       LOS F represents jammed conditions where the intersection is over capacity and
       acceptable gaps for unsignalized intersections in the mainline traffic flow are minimal.
       At signalized intersections, average vehicle delays exceed 80 seconds. At unsignalized
       intersections, average delays exceed 50 seconds.
C2. Year 2013 Existing Traffic Operations ­ No Improvements
Exhibit 3-3 shows the Year 2013 existing traffic (no development) peak hour operating conditions
at the study area intersections. The Year 2013 existing traffic analysis was conducted using the
existing intersection geometrics (Exhibit 3-1) and existing traffic signal phasing/timing (see
Appendix A).
As shown in Exhibit 3-3, all movements at the study area intersections operate acceptably under
existing traffic volumes.
PART D ­ ROADWAY LEVEL OF SERVICE
A roadway capacity analysis was performed for Nagawicka Road to determine the sufficiency
for the roadway to accommodate existing traffic. The analysis was performed with the following
parameters:
           AM Peak parameters used (highest volume observed);
           Shoulder width: 1-foot;
           Lane width: 11-feet;
           Directional split: 57/43;
           Peak hour factor: 0.56;
           Trucks & buses: 3%;
           RV vehicles: 0%;
           Percent no-passing lanes: 100%;
           Access density: 20 per mile;
           Class II highway;
           Measured speed: 33 mph; and
           Observed flow rate: 235 vph.
Traffic volume was increased incrementally to determine threshold values for the various levels
of service. Based on the results, the levels of service for two-way traffic flows are as follows:
                                                LOS A < 118 vph
                                   118 vph  LOS B < 251 vph
                                   251 vph  LOS C < 538 vph
                                   538 vph  LOS D < 1,008 vph
                                 1,008 vph  LOS E < 1,665 vph
                                 1,665 vph  LOS F
With a two-way traffic flow of 235 vph, Nagawicka Road currently operates at LOS B, can
accommodate approximately 2.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS C/D threshold,
and can accommodate approximately 4.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS D/E
threshold.

                      CHAPTER IV ­ FORECASTED TRAFFIC
PART A ­ SITE TRAFFIC FORECASTING
To address any potential future traffic impacts at the study area intersections, it is necessary to
identify the hourly volume of traffic generated by anticipated development. The traffic volumes
expected to be generated by Christian Chapel & School are based on the size and type of the
proposed use and on trip rates as published in the Institute of Transportation Engineers' (ITE)
Trip Generation Manual, Ninth Edition, 2012.
A1. Trip Generation
The trip generation table for Christian Chapel & School is shown in Exhibit 4-1. As shown, the
full build-out of the Christian Chapel & School is expected to result in approximately 335 new
trips (185 in/150 out) during a typical weekday morning pear hour of school arrival, 220 new
trips (105 in/115 out) during a typical weekday midday peak hour of school dismissal, and 110
new trips (55 in/55 out) during a typical weekday evening peak hour.
A2. Mode Split
Pedestrians and bicyclists may use their respective modes to access Christian Chapel & School.
However, these additional modes are expected to make up a small portion of the overall trips
to/from the study area. Therefore, for the purpose of this TIA, all trips to/from the proposed
development site were assumed to occur via motor vehicle.
A3. Trip Distribution
The trip distribution for Christian Chapel & School was determined based on existing travel
patterns in the area, as well as on the expected regional influence area of the Lake Country area.
The trip distribution is shown in Exhibit 4-1 and is summarized below.
       Scenario One (Without Connection):
        55 percent to/from the north on STH 83;
           35 percent to/from the south on STH 83;
           10 percent to/from the east on Cardinal Lane;
       Scenario Two (With Connection):
        50 percent to/from the north on STH 83;
           30 percent to/from the south on STH 83;
           10 percent to/from the east on Cardinal Lane;
            5 percent to/from the north on Nagawicka Road; and
            5 percent to/from the south on Nagawicka Road.
A4. Trip Assignment
The new trips expected to be generated by Christian Chapel & School were assigned to the study
area intersections based on the trip distribution previously summarized. The Christian Chapel &
School scenario one (without connection) trip assignment is shown in Exhibit 4-2a. The
Christian Chapel & School scenario two (with connection) trip assignment is shown in Exhibit 4-
2b.
If a future collector street connection is made between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway
(i.e. scenario two), it is estimated that traffic to/from the south on Nagawicka Road will increase
by approximately 10-percent due to motorists from STH 83 who will now utilize the new street
TADI                                                                                             10
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                        April 10, 2013

corridor rather than using existing southerly east-west streets. The Year 2013 existing traffic
redistribution volumes under scenario two (with connection) are shown in Exhibit 4-3.
PART B ­ BUILD TRAFFIC
The Year 2013 scenario one (without connection) build traffic volumes were determined by
adding the Year 2013 existing traffic volumes (Exhibit 3-2) to the Christian Chapel & School
scenario one trip assignment (Exhibit 4-2a). The Year 2013 scenario one build traffic volumes
are shown in Exhibit 4-4a.
The Year 2013 scenario two (with connection) build traffic volumes were determined by adding
the Year 2013 existing traffic volumes (Exhibit 3-2) to the Christian Chapel & School scenario
two trip assignment (Exhibit 4-2b) and the anticipated Year 2013 existing traffic redistribution
volumes (Exhibit 4-3). The Year 2013 scenario two build traffic volumes are shown in Exhibit
4-4b.

         CHAPTER V ­ TRAFFIC AND IMPROVEMENT ANALYSIS
PART A ­ SITE ACCESS
Primary access to the Christian Chapel & School is planned to STH 83 via an extension of
Cardinal Lane.
The City of Delafield 2030 Comprehensive Plan envisions a future collector street connecting
Cardinal Lane to Faire Lakes Parkway. For the purpose of this study, two scenarios were
developed:
       Under Scenario One, a future collector street connection does not exist. All access is
       accommodated via STH 83.
       Under Scenario Two, a future secondary access is assumed to Nagawicka Road via a
       connection of Faire Lakes Parkway to Cardinal Lane.
A recommendation regarding the two scenarios is summarized at the end of Chapter I and of
Chapter VI.
PART B ­ CAPACITY LEVEL OF SERVICE ANALYSIS
B1. Traffic Operating Conditions ­ No Improvements
Exhibit 5-1 shows the Year 2013 build traffic (with Christian Chapel & School) peak hour
operating conditions at the study area intersections under both scenario one (without connection)
and scenario two (with connection). The Year 2013 build traffic analysis was conducted using
the existing intersection geometrics (Exhibit 3-1) and existing traffic signal phasing/timing (see
Appendix A).
As shown in Exhibit 5-1, all movements at the study area intersections are expected to continue
to operate acceptably under build traffic volumes without improvements the study area
intersections.
B2. Traffic Operating Conditions ­ With Improvements
Improvements to accommodate build traffic (with Christian Chapel & School) are summarized in
Chapter VI and are recommended to improve the safety of motorists in the study area with the
proposed Christian Chapel & School built-out.
As shown in Exhibit 5-2, all movements at the study area intersections are expected to continue
to operate acceptably under build traffic volumes with the safety improvements recommended at
the study area intersections.
PART C ­ QUEUEING ANALYSIS
To estimate storage length requirements for turn bays at the study area intersections with
improvements, a queuing analysis has been conducted. Note that the 50th percentile and 95th
percentile probable queue lengths were used for the design of turn bay storage at the
intersections.
Exhibit 5-3a shows the Year 2013 scenario one (without connection) build traffic expected
maximum queues with improvements to accommodate development.
Exhibit 5-3b shows the Year 2013 scenario two (with connection) build traffic expected
maximum queues with improvements to accommodate development.




TADI                                                                                             12
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                       April 10, 2013

PART D ­ SPEED STUDY
A speed study was performed along Nagawicka Road from Faire Lakes Parkway in mid-March
of 2013 during the morning peak period with dry pavement. The data for the speed study is
included in Appendix A.
The speed study results indicate that the 50th percentile speed along Nagawicka Road
approaching Faire Lakes Parkway is 30 mph while the 85th percentile speed is 33 mph. The
results suggest that the existing posted speed limit of 30 mph on Nagawicka Road is reasonable.
PART E ­ INTERSECTION SIGHT DISTANCE STUDY
The party responsible for designing roadways and intersections will be responsible for cross-
checking, verifying and designing for all applicable sight distances.
Intersection sight distance (ISD) was checked along Nagawicka Road at the existing Faire Lakes
Parkway intersection. The ISD study was performed using a design speed of 35 mph.
Calculations for proper ISD at a design speed of 35 mph are included in Appendix D. Exhibits
5-4a through 5-4c show the results of the ISD study.
The field checks indicate that the right-out maneuver (looking south towards northbound
oncoming traffic) from Faire Lakes Parkway, and the left-in maneuver (looking south towards
northbound oncoming traffic) from Nagawicka Road, do not meet the minimum ISD
requirements (see Exhibits 5-4a and 5-4b). The ISD is not met due to trees that line the
southwest side of the curve. It is recommended to clear all trees, brush and other obstructions
from within the ISD envelope.

         CHAPTER VI ­ RECOMMENDATIONS AND CONCLUSION
PART A ­ RECOMMENDATIONS
The study area intersections were analyzed based on the procedures set forth in the 2000
Highway Capacity Manual (HCM). Intersection operation is defined by "level of service".
Level of Service (LOS) is a quantitative measure that refers to the overall quality of flow at an
intersection ranging from very good, represented by LOS `A', to very poor, represented by LOS
`F'. For the purpose of this study, and as is standard for use in the WisDOT Southeast Region,
LOS D or better was used to define desirable peak hour operating conditions.
A1. Existing Traffic Recommended Improvements
The following improvements are recommended to accommodate the Year 2013 existing (without
development) traffic volumes. These improvements are in addition to conditions as they
currently exist and are recommended regardless of any new development in the area.
Improvements are for jurisdictional consideration and are not legally binding. WisDOT and the
City of Delafield reserve the right to determine alternative solutions.
       STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
           No improvements are expected to be necessary.
       Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway
           TADI performed a speed study along Nagawicka Road at Faire Lakes Parkway.
             The 85th percentile speed was found to be 33-mph. The results suggest that the
             existing posted speed limit of 30 mph on Nagawicka Road is reasonable.
               TADI performed an intersection sight distance (ISD) study for the Nagawicka
               Road intersection with Faire Lakes Parkway. The study revealed that ISD is not
               currently provided from Faire Lakes Parkway to Nagawicka Road. It is
               recommended to clear all trees, brush and other obstructions from within the ISD
               envelope.
               TADI learned that a crash involving more than one fatality occurred at the
               intersection due to a loss of vehicle control within the last one to three years, and
               another fatality occurred at the intersection approximately fifteen years ago. To
               improve the safety of the intersection, countermeasures such as wider shoulders
               with rumble strips, "curve ahead" signs, and/or a lighted intersection should be
               considered within the intersection influence area.
A2. Build Traffic Recommended Improvements
The following improvements, shown in Exhibit 1-3, are recommended to accommodate the Year
2013 build (with Christian Chapel & School) traffic volumes regardless of whether or not a
collector street connection is made between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway. These
improvements are in addition to conditions as they currently exist. Improvements are for
jurisdictional consideration and are not legally binding. WisDOT and the City of Delafield
reserve the right to determine alternative solutions.
       STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
           Construct a right-turn lane on the STH 83 southbound approach.
               Provide two lanes on the Cardinal Lane eastbound approach, including one left-
               turn lane and a shared through/right-turn lane. Align the center of the eastbound


TADI                                                                                              14
Christian Chapel & School TIA - Delafield, WI                                        April 10, 2013

               left-turn lane with the center of the existing westbound left-turn lane to improve
               sight distance for left-turn motorists at the intersection.
       Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway
           No improvements are expected to be necessary beyond those recommended to
             accommodate existing traffic volumes.
       Other Considerations
           Install stop signs to control the northbound and southbound frontage road
              approaches to Cardinal Lane.
               Roadways to/from the development may be constructed as two-lane undivided
               facilities.
               It is recommended to move forward with the proposed development without the
               collector roadway connection between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway.
                   o A collector connection is not necessary, as the connection would not
                     provide a substantial benefit to the proposed Christian Chapel & School,
                     to the STH 83 & Cardinal Lane intersection, or the Nagawicka Road &
                     Faire Lakes Parkway intersection.
                   o A collector connection is expected to increase traffic along Nagawicka
                     Road at Faire Lakes Parkway rather than relieve it.
                   o Nagawicka Road currently operates at LOS B and has excess capacity to
                     accommodate 2.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS C/D
                     threshold. With land along Nagawicka Road nearly fully built-out today,
                     future development opportunities along Nagawicka Road are not expected
                     to result in traffic concerns that would drive the need for a collector
                     connection.
PART B ­ CONCLUSION
All movements at the study area intersections are expected to operate safely and efficiently with
the identified recommended improvements.
It is recommended to move forward with the proposed development without the collector
roadway connection between Cardinal Lane and Faire Lakes Parkway, for the following reasons:
       A collector connection is not necessary, as the connection would not provide a substantial
       benefit to the proposed Christian Chapel & School, to the STH 83 & Cardinal Lane
       intersection, or the Nagawicka Road & Faire Lakes Parkway intersection.
       A collector connection is expected to increase traffic along Nagawicka Road at Faire
       Lakes Parkway rather than relieve it.
       Nagawicka Road currently operates at LOS B and has excess capacity to accommodate
       2.3-times as much traffic before reaching the LOS C/D threshold. With land along
       Nagawicka Road nearly fully built-out today, future development opportunities along
       Nagawicka Road are not expected to result in traffic concerns that would drive the need
       for a collector connection.
